## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t. Nonlinear oscillators extend the simple harmonic case with anharmonic restoring forces, nonlinear damping, and/or external driving.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (unforced): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (nonlinear damping)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic external forcing)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing with driving)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order anharmonicity)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (amplitude-dependent frequency)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity nonlinearity)
- Nonlinear damping + Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v**3 (combined nonlinearities)
- Coulomb-like friction: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (c2 + c3 * x**2) (position-dependent damping)
- General polynomial: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v + c4 * v * x (mixed polynomial terms)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) preserve oscillator symmetry; even powers (x**2) break it, suggesting asymmetric potentials
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v represent linear dissipation; terms like x**2 * v or v**3 indicate nonlinear (amplitude-dependent) energy exchange
- Explicit time dependence via sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicates externally driven systems; absence of t suggests autonomous dynamics
- Product terms x*v indicate phase-space coupling and often arise in self-excited oscillators (van der Pol type)
- If acceleration depends only on x (not v or t), the system is conservative with a potential energy V(x) where dv_dt = -dV/dx
- Cubic restoring force x**3 with same sign as linear term x indicates hardening spring; opposite sign indicates softening spring with potential escape
- Parametric excitation appears as multiplicative time modulation of position-dependent terms, distinct from additive forcing
- Negative linear damping (positive coefficient of v) combined with cubic velocity saturation (negative v**3) characterizes limit cycle oscillators
